A general <a href="/wiki/Systems_collapse" class="mw-redirect" title="Systems collapse">systems collapse</a> has been put forward as an explanation for the reversals in culture that occurred between the <a href="/wiki/Urnfield_culture" title="Urnfield culture">Urnfield culture</a> of the 13th and 12th centuries BC and the rise of the Celtic <a href="/wiki/Hallstatt_culture" title="Hallstatt culture">Hallstatt culture</a> in the 9th and 10th centuries BC.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Pandemic">Pandemic</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_Bronze_Age_collapse&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Pandemic"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Recent evidence suggests the collapse of the cultures in Mycenaean Greece, Hittite Anatolia, and the Levant may have been precipitated or worsened by the arrival of an early and now-extinct strain of the <a href="/wiki/Bubonic_plague" title="Bubonic plague">bubonic plague</a> brought from central Asia by the Sea Peoples or other migrating groups.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Volcanoes">Volcanoes</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_Bronze_Age_collapse&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Volcanoes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Some Egyptologists have dated the <a href="/wiki/Hekla_3_eruption" title="Hekla 3 eruption">Hekla 3 volcanic eruption</a> in Iceland to <a href="/wiki/1159_BC" class="mw-redirect" title="1159 BC">1159 BC</a> and blamed it for famines under <a href="/wiki/Ramesses_III" title="Ramesses III">Ramesses III</a> during the wider Bronze Age collapse.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The event is thought to have caused a <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_winter" title="Volcanic winter">volcanic winter</a>. Other estimated dates for the Hekla 3 eruption range from 1021 (±130)<sup id="cite_ref-baker_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baker-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> to 1135 BC (±130)<sup id="cite_ref-baker_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baker-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and 929 (±34).<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other scholars prefer the neutral and vague "3000 <a href="/wiki/Before_Present" title="Before Present">BP</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Warfare">Warfare</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_Bronze_Age_collapse&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Warfare"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ancient_warfare" title="Ancient warfare">Ancient warfare</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Robert_Drews" title="Robert Drews">Robert Drews</a> argues<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDrews1993192ff_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDrews1993192ff-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> for the appearance of massed <a href="/wiki/Infantry" title="Infantry">infantry</a>, using newly developed weapons and armour, such as <a href="/wiki/Casting_(metalworking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Casting (metalworking)">cast</a> rather than <a href="/wiki/Forging" title="Forging">forged</a> spearheads and <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age_sword#Europe" title="Bronze Age sword">long swords</a>, a revolutionizing cut-and-thrust weapon,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDrews1993194_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDrews1993194-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Javelin" title="Javelin">javelins</a>. The appearance of bronze foundries suggests "that mass production of bronze artefacts was suddenly important in the Aegean". For example, <a href="/wiki/Homer" title="Homer">Homer</a> uses "spears" as a <a href="/wiki/Metonymy" title="Metonymy">metonym</a> for "warriors".
</p><p>Such new weaponry, in the hands of large numbers of "running <a href="/wiki/Skirmisher" title="Skirmisher">skirmishers</a>", who could swarm and cut down a chariot army, would destabilize states that were based upon the use of chariots by the ruling class. That would precipitate an abrupt social collapse as raiders began to conquer, loot and burn cities.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDrews1993_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDrews1993-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Aftermath">Aftermath</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Late_Bronze_Age_collapse&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Aftermath"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Robert Drews described the collapse as "arguably the worst disaster in ancient history, even more calamitous than the <a href="/wiki/Collapse_of_the_Western_Roman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Collapse of the Western Roman Empire">collapse of the Western Roman Empire</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Cultural memories of the disaster told of a "lost <a href="/wiki/Golden_age" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden age">golden age</a>". For example, <a href="/wiki/Hesiod" title="Hesiod">Hesiod</a> spoke of Ages of Gold, Silver, and Bronze, separated from the cruel modern Age of Iron by the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Heroic_Age" title="Greek Heroic Age">Age of Heroes</a>. Rodney Castleden suggests that memories of the Bronze Age collapse influenced <a href="/wiki/Plato" title="Plato">Plato</a>'s story of <a href="/wiki/Atlantis" title="Atlantis">Atlantis</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Timaeus_(dialogue)" title="Timaeus (dialogue)">Timaeus</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Critias_(dialogue)" title="Critias (dialogue)">Critias</a></i>.
</p><p>Only a few powerful states survived the Bronze Age collapse, particularly <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyria</a> (albeit temporarily weakened), the New Kingdom of Egypt (also weakened), the <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenician</a> city-states and <a href="/wiki/Elam" title="Elam">Elam</a>. Even among these comparative survivors, success was mixed. By the end of the 12th century BC, Elam waned after its defeat by <a href="/wiki/Nebuchadnezzar_I" title="Nebuchadnezzar I">Nebuchadnezzar I</a>, who briefly revived Babylonian fortunes before suffering a series of defeats by the Assyrians. After the death of <a href="/wiki/Ashur-bel-kala" title="Ashur-bel-kala">Ashur-bel-kala</a> in 1056 BC, Assyria declined for a century. Its empire shrank significantly by 1020 BC, apparently leaving it in control only of the areas in its immediate vicinity, although its heartland remained well-defended. By the time of <a href="/wiki/Wenamun" class="mw-redirect" title="Wenamun">Wenamun</a>, Phoenicia had regained independence from Egypt.
</p><p>Gradually, by the end of the ensuing Dark Age, remnants of the Hittites coalesced into small <a href="/wiki/Syro-Hittite_states" title="Syro-Hittite states">Syro-Hittite states</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cilicia" title="Cilicia">Cilicia</a> and in the Levant, where the new states were composed of mixed Hittite and <a href="/wiki/Arameans" title="Arameans">Aramean</a> polities. Beginning in the mid-10th century BC, a series of small Aramean kingdoms formed in the Levant, and the <a href="/wiki/Philistines" title="Philistines">Philistines</a> settled in southern Canaan, where Canaanite speakers had coalesced into a number of polities such as <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(united_monarchy)" title="Kingdom of Israel (united monarchy)">Israel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moab" title="Moab">Moab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edom" title="Edom">Edom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ammon" title="Ammon">Ammon</a>.
</p>
